2f:["$","p",null,{"style":{"fontSize":"1rem","color":"var(--text-body)","lineHeight":1.75,"marginBottom":"1.25em","marginTop":0},"children":"Safety failures in deployed robot systems rarely trace to a single failure mode. They\nemerge from the interaction between multiple imperfect components: a policy that has\nlearned a slightly incorrect dynamics model, a sensor that drifts over time, a contact\ngeometry that is slightly different from training, and a control loop that has no\nmechanism to detect that these errors have compounded to a dangerous extent."}]
30:["$","p",null,{"style":{"fontSize":"1rem","color":"var(--text-body)","lineHeight":1.75,"marginBottom":"1.25em","marginTop":0},"children":["This systems character has a fundamental implication: ",["$","strong",null,{"style":{"color":"var(--text-strong)","fontWeight":600},"children":"safety cannot be fully learned"}],".\nA policy that learns safe behavior by observing demonstrations will inherit the safety\nassumptions implicit in those demonstrations. Demonstrations collected by skilled human\noperators avoid dangerous configurations because the operator's judgment prevents them;\nthe policy learns to avoid those configurations on its memorized training trajectories\nbut has no explicit model of why they are dangerous or how to avoid them in novel\nconfigurations. Safety must therefore be enforced ",["$","strong",null,{"style":{"color":"var(--text-strong)","fontWeight":600},"children":"outside"}]," the learned policy, through\nformal constraints and monitors that are designed against the robot's physical\nspecifications rather than inferred from data."]}]

36:["$","p",null,{"style":{"fontSize":"1rem","color":"var(--text-body)","lineHeight":1.75,"marginBottom":"1.25em","marginTop":0},"children":["More sophisticated safety filters enforce ",["$","strong",null,{"style":{"color":"var(--text-strong)","fontWeight":600},"children":"collision avoidance"}]," and ",["$","strong",null,{"style":{"color":"var(--text-strong)","fontWeight":600},"children":"workspace exclusion\nzones"}],". Forward kinematics maps the joint configuration to a set of link poses, and\ncollision checking evaluates whether any link pose intersects a forbidden zone (table surface,\noperator exclusion volume, adjacent equipment). If the policy's proposed action would move\na link into a forbidden zone, the filter projects the action to the boundary of the\npermissible workspace. Efficient collision checking using signed distance fields or geometric\nprimitives can run at 1 kHz control rates."]}]

54:["$","p",null,{"style":{"fontSize":"1rem","color":"var(--text-body)","lineHeight":1.75,"marginBottom":"1.25em","marginTop":0},"children":[["$","strong",null,{"style":{"color":"var(--text-strong)","fontWeight":600},"children":"Rare contact events"}]," are systematically underrepresented in demonstration datasets.\nDatasets collected from skilled human operators contain few examples of unexpected collisions,\nnear-singular grasps, or objects tipping unexpectedly — because the operators avoided\nthem. 76:["$","p",null,{"style":{"fontSize":"1rem","color":"var(--text-body)","lineHeight":1.75,"marginBottom":"1.25em","marginTop":0},"children":"Safety in robot deployment is a systems problem requiring safety enforcement at multiple\nlayers, not just good policy training. Safety filters intercept unsafe actions before\nexecution; CBF-QP provides formal forward-invariance guarantees for defined constraint sets\nby solving a real-time quadratic program that minimally modifies the policy's proposed\naction. Covariate shift, rare contact events, and control latency are the primary failure\nmodes in deployed manipulation systems; each has targeted monitoring and mitigation\nstrategies. Runtime monitoring of action magnitude, constraint margins, policy uncertainty,\nand task progress enables early failure detection before damage occurs. Fallback mechanisms\nranging from action clipping to full controller handoff provide graceful degradation. The\nprinciple that safety is enforced externally rather than learned internally applies equally\nto robot policies and language model alignment."}]

138:["$","li",null,{"style":{"marginBottom":"0.35em","fontSize":"1rem"},"children":[["$","strong",null,{"style":{"color":"var(--text-strong)","fontWeight":600},"children":"Shielded RL."}]," When the backup engages, the executed action is not the policy's proposal, so crediting the policy with the backup's outcome gives misleading gradients — frequent early engagement means almost no correct signal near the boundary, and the policy never learns good boundary behavior. Curriculum: begin with a conservative shield (engages readily for safety) and gradually relax the shielding threshold as the policy improves so it experiences near-boundary states — crediting only the policy's own actions (off-policy correction) — tightening again only if safety degrades."]}]
